<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_fbda6ad2-4dc3-44aa-b99b-ed36464663ab'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2562495432546341694">A chance meeting on a train to Tokyo sends two girls named Nana on a collision course with destiny!<br/><br/>Nana "Hachi" Komatsu hopes that moving to Tokyo will help her make a clean start and leave her capricious love life behind her.   <span id="freeText2562495432546341694" style="display:none">A chance meeting on a train to Tokyo sends two girls named Nana on a collision course with destiny!<br /><br />Nana "Hachi" Komatsu hopes that moving to Tokyo will help her make a clean start and leave her capricious love life behind her. Nana Osaki, who arrives in the city at the same time, has plans to score big in the world of rock'n'roll. Although these two young women come from different backgrounds, they quickly become best friends in a whirlwind world of sex, music, fashion, gossip and all-night parties!<br /><br />Nana Komatsu is a young woman who's endured an unending string of boyfriend problems. Moving to Tokyo, she's hoping to take control of her life and put all those messy misadventures behind her. She's looking for love and she's hoping to find it in the big city.<br /><br />Nana Osaki, on the other hand, is cool, confident and focused. She swaggers into town and proceeds to kick down the doors to Tokyo's underground punk scene. She's got a dream and won't give up until she becomes Japan's No. 1 rock'n'roll superstar.<br /><br />This is the story of two 20-year-old women who share the same name. Even though they come from completely different backgrounds, they somehow meet and become best friends. The world of <b>
  <i>Nana</i>
</b> is a world exploding with sex, music, fashion, gossip and all-night parties.</span>

<div id="review_30662023" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30662023" />
    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1443874-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/30662023?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/1443874-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer30662023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1523702023451876189">A review of the entire manga series. No real plot spoilers, but very vague references to future events. <br/><br/>My all-time favorite manga. The story of two girls, punk rocker Nana Oosaki ("big" Nana) and girly Nana Komatsu ("small" Nana, known in the rest of the story as Hachi), who meet on a train to Tokyo and become the best of friends. Nana's dream is to become a famous punk singer, Hachi's to live with her boyfriend, Shouji. <br/><br/>The first volume deals with the girls' past - Hachi's normal, fairly happy</span>
  <span id="freeText1523702023451876189" style="display:none">A review of the entire manga series. No real plot spoilers, but very vague references to future events. <br /><br />My all-time favorite manga. The story of two girls, punk rocker Nana Oosaki ("big" Nana) and girly Nana Komatsu ("small" Nana, known in the rest of the story as Hachi), who meet on a train to Tokyo and become the best of friends. Nana's dream is to become a famous punk singer, Hachi's to live with her boyfriend, Shouji. <br /><br />The first volume deals with the girls' past - Hachi's normal, fairly happy adolescence (not counting disastrous love affairs, a character hallmark); and Nana's harder-edged, more tragic existence. It also introduces most of the wonderful supporting cast - Junko and Kyosuke; Yasu!, Nobu, and Ren. <br /><br />Subsequent volumes highlight how well Nana and Hachi's divergent personalities complement each other, and their growing bond. What I like best about the series is how the characters develop - flighty, shallow Hachi becomes the pillar of emotional strength; and independent, tough Nana is revealed to be extremely vulnerable. Hachi is my favorite character - although not introduced in the most positive light, her strength and positive attitude when karma comes back around is commendable. <br /><br />Another thing I love is the narration at the beginning and end of chapters, highlighting Nana and Hachi's bond and foreshadowing a tragic future, which is later partially revealed in flash-forwards. Instead of giving plot away, the future hints are played out like a mystery story, giving small pieces to solve like a puzzle. Much like <i> Lost </i> in a way, plot-structure-wise, flashbacks are also used to give character depth, while the flashforwards and the present rush to meet each other. <br /><br />There's a huge amount of fantasy in their lives in Tokyo, even aside from the connections to the famous group Trapnest. I've lived in a "big" apartment on the outskirts of Tokyo, and the entire place could of fit twice into Room 707's living area. And I don't think there's a single apartment in the city going for a monthly rent of 750 yen, yet alone a giant place like that. (And I'm not buying the whole "no elevator" excuse - you walk a hell of a lot more than seven flights of stairs in daily Tokyo life.) But the fantasy is a big part of <i> Nana's </i> charm - it's life the way you wish it could be lived, not the way it actually is. <br /><br />The decidedly Western apartment and style of living should translate very well with American audiences. And even the style remains in the translation - it's not just western, it's a beautiful 60's-esque retro. The apartment and most of Hachi's clothing looks straight out of <i> Breakfast at Tiffany's</i>. And Nana always looks like she walked straight off a Vivenne Westwood catwalk. Yazawa's signature fashion and style is on full display here. <br /><br />Another thing on full display is Yazawa's well-developed characters - but unlike, say, <i>Paradise Kiss</i>, these characters are really likable. You root for them from the moment you meet them. And the plot is heads and tails above previous efforts - you can't stop reading once you start. The only complaint I have is some of the later chapters' over-focus on the Trapnest members - the manga is called <i> Nana </i>, after all. <br /><br />There's a reason why <i> Nana </i> is one of the most popular shoujo manga of all time in Japan. Even the names are carefully selected, with several levels - "Nana" meaning seven, "Hachi" meaning both eight and the loyal dog Hachiko, and how the bad luck connotation the number seven implies in Japan follows the two girls. That and the "Demon Lord." <br /><br />I can't recommend this series enough. Although one suggestion - try to locate the scanlations. The English translation is horrible, an abomination. The translators decided to "Americanize" the characters' speech, and ended up with a horrid hip-hopish grammatically incorrect sludge that no <i>American</i> young adult speaks in, yet alone Japanese characters. It's really a shame. Reading the series' English translation might ruin it for you. If you like it, please buy at least a couple volumes to support it - but don't read them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1523702023451876189" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13380652254198699898">This review is for volumes 1-21, so there may be some spoilers.<br/><br/>I was excited when I found out my library had this series, because that meant I could finally finish it! I'd read volume 1 years ago, but it was right around the time I stopped buying manga, and so I never completed the series.<br/><br/>And then I found out from Kat the series isn't even complete!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457391403ra/18354141.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This series is about two bands who rise to popularity in Japan and the struggles that go along with fame. It's also about the friendship between two </span>
  <span id="freeText13380652254198699898" style="display:none">This review is for volumes 1-21, so there may be some spoilers.<br><br>I was excited when I found out my library had this series, because that meant I could finally finish it! I'd read volume 1 years ago, but it was right around the time I stopped buying manga, and so I never completed the series.<br><br>And then I found out from Kat the series isn't even complete!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457391403ra/18354141.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This series is about two bands who rise to popularity in Japan and the struggles that go along with fame. It's also about the friendship between two young women named Nana (which ended up being the best thing about this whole story).<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457391403ra/18354142.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked this series, but I could have liked it a lot more without the constant drama and the characters making decisions I hated. My main example of this is Hachi's relationship with Takumi. What the actual fuck??? I couldn't tell if Yazawa meant for us to hate him or like him, because he did terrible things <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(isolating Hachi, forcing himself on her, being rude to her, etc.) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> yet was shown in a sympathetic light over and over again.<br><br>Takumi's relationship with Reira confused the fuck out of me, and I hated it. Takumi can fuck right off with his hot, sociopathic self.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457391403ra/18354143.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hachi was my favorite character (with Shin as a close second), although I hate what she went through in order to find the tiniest bit of happiness. Takumi didn't deserve her. I don't prefer Nobu, though. I actually ship Hachi with the photographer! (I forgot his name.)<br><br>Yazawa does some of my favorite manga artwork, and I wish more of her series were readily available to me. However, now I need a break from having read an entire manga series straight through without any breaks. *wipes brow*<br><br><b>
  <i>Making your dreams come true and being happy... Why are they two separate things?</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457391541ra/18354162.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review159618609">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_163607300" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/163607300" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3212850-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491430066p2/3212850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/163607300?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/3212850-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3212850-liz?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer163607300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14580288225251742706">Nana, Volume 1 is the first volume out of a 21 volume series written by Ai Yazawa. Volume 1 introduces us to Nana Kumatsu, Nana Osaki, and Junko (Nana Kumatsu’s best friend, she’s pretty much a bonus to the series). The manga shows us these three girls lives (but mainly the two Nanas). Nana Kumatsu is this melodramatic and quite boy crazy girl. She follows her heart and a lot of the time, it gets her into trouble. Nana Osaki is a very dark and serious personality. She’s the lead singer of her ba</span>
  <span id="freeText14580288225251742706" style="display:none">Nana, Volume 1 is the first volume out of a 21 volume series written by Ai Yazawa. Volume 1 introduces us to Nana Kumatsu, Nana Osaki, and Junko (Nana Kumatsu’s best friend, she’s pretty much a bonus to the series). The manga shows us these three girls lives (but mainly the two Nanas). Nana Kumatsu is this melodramatic and quite boy crazy girl. She follows her heart and a lot of the time, it gets her into trouble. Nana Osaki is a very dark and serious personality. She’s the lead singer of her band and is in love with one of the guitarists. Both girls have to make very big decisions as far as growing up and deciding whether or not to move to Tokyo. <br /><br />The book is split in half as far as the stories of these girls, so it’s not flipping back and forth between the two characters. I thought that that was quite helpful as to not confuse the readers (even though the two Nanas are quite different in looks). That being said, both stories and plots were well written. There were times when Nana K would get really depressed and quite crazy, but it is explained quite well. Even though she has a bubbly personality, she’s had some very rough times. Nana O’s storyline was more sexual and more about her reaction to this boy leaving her for a bigger opportunity. <br /><br />That doesn’t seem like much in the way of story, but this volume is more to introduce us to characters. That way, we get to know them a bit before the story really starts. I thought the overall writing was very well done. It hit some serious subjects but didn’t dwell on it too much so that it’s still a light read.<br /><br />I liked the setting for Nana K. She was right in the middle of everything, which showed both how she was geographically and how she was psychologically. <br /><br />I would recommend this volume to anyone in their late teens (16+) and beyond. There is some mature and serious content. I would also recommend it to anyone who doesn’t have patience for a novel but would like to start reading more. This manga had some good story and plot and character development, but it isn’t a long read (180 pages at most). Please be warned that you read manga right-to-left rather than how in English, we read left-to-right. <br /><br />As far as rating, I was told by a few girls and a few guys that I would like this volume (and series). I would definitely give it a solid A (95/100). Seriously, good stuff. I’m considering reading at least a few more volumes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14580288225251742706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_880654323" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/880654323" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/880654323?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer880654323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10571052444370365013"><i>Nana #1</i> consists of two stories, one following a sparkly high school girl named Nana, and one story following a punk lead vocalist Nana. From here on I'll be referring to them as Barbie and Punky. <br/><br/>We start out with Barbie, who has an affair with a grown man she knows almost nothing about. When he ends things, she's having a hard time getting over him. Barbie always falls head over heels for older guys, and usually within the first ten seconds of meeting them. Influenced by her best friend, she t</span>
  <span id="freeText10571052444370365013" style="display:none"><i>Nana #1</i> consists of two stories, one following a sparkly high school girl named Nana, and one story following a punk lead vocalist Nana. From here on I'll be referring to them as Barbie and Punky. <br /><br />We start out with Barbie, who has an affair with a grown man she knows almost nothing about. When he ends things, she's having a hard time getting over him. Barbie always falls head over heels for older guys, and usually within the first ten seconds of meeting them. Influenced by her best friend, she tries being best friends with a guy for once.<br /><br />Punky is the archetypical character with a bad past. She sings in a band, where her boyfriend is the lead guitar. Her boyfriend has his big break, and leaves for Tokyo, leaving Punky behind. She is forced to make some tough choices.<br /><br />Although Barbie is superficial and annoying at times, I liked her part of the story best. Punky's just didn't have the same amount of humour and heart. I felt that Punky didn't have anything that made her unique in any way, and I didn't feel invested in her story. <br /><br />Some issues I had with the story probably stem from the fact that I know absolutely nothing about Japanese culture, and some story lines just got a bit weird for me. At one point a male character doesn't say "I love you" to a female character, because that's apparently the Western way, but instead just kinda says it by kissing her. I'm not much of a romantic, but I did find this a bit lame. It's easy to kiss someone, but it takes balls to tell someone you love them. But I guess that kind of sentiment doesn't agree with the Japanese view of masculinity. <br /><br /><i>Nana</i> is entertaining, especially Barbie's half of the novel. I might read a few more in the series, as my library has them, but I'm not sure whether I'm hooked enough to read the full 21 volumes of this manga. Also, the author didn't finish the series, and might never write the last volume. I don't want to become invested in a series that might not get an ending. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10571052444370365013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1585795563" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

This is enough for them to decide to move in together the next time they see each other. <s>This and cheap rent, of course.</s><br /><br />Goth Nana is more confident and girly Nana is more childish but both of them are new to independant life and the big city. Nanas have a great dynamics and after just a few interactions I feel that they're going to impact each other a lot. <s>Also, I ship them already ups... I'm going to suffer because it's not yuri but girly Nana has spent more than one page admiring goth Nana's looks so..</s><br /><br />I didn't like girly Nana's boyfriend. He seemed very flat and annoying. ALSO, his friends looked like siblings a bit? I was SHOOK that they're dating.. <br /><br />This seems like something that will become more serious and sad as it goes but I can't take it 100% serious with those noodle legs..     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1487008518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1487008518" />
    <a title="Andy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24123282-andy"><img alt="Andy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434629539p2/24123282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1487008518?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy " href="/user/show/24123282-andy">Andy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Shoujo lovers looking for life bonding friendships with cutesy yet gritty moments. </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=family-like-matters">family-like-matters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=favourites-m">favourites-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=friendships">friendships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=badboy-tatoos-rings">badboy-tatoos-rings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=drama-a-lot-of-shit-went-down">drama-a-lot-of-shit-went-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=best-of-sarcasm">best-of-sarcasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=girl-on-cover">girl-on-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24123282-andy?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1487008518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9522064373865274209"><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451551713ra/17557714.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/> <b>The Japanese incarnation of Lisabeth Salander. </b> That's what I first thought of when I saw punk-gothic, band playing Nana raising an eyebrow at the over gushy chatterbox sitting next to her. Who also happens to be named Nana...<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451551713i/17557715._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>When two utterly different girls with two completely divergent personalities find themselves sitting next to each other on a 5 hour train journey to Tokyo what else is there to do but talk especially, since both of them share the same age, direction and name? Nana howeve</span>
  <span id="freeText9522064373865274209" style="display:none"><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451551713ra/17557714.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <b>The Japanese incarnation of Lisabeth Salander. </b> That's what I first thought of when I saw punk-gothic, band playing Nana raising an eyebrow at the over gushy chatterbox sitting next to her. Who also happens to be named Nana...<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1451551713i/17557715._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When two utterly different girls with two completely divergent personalities find themselves sitting next to each other on a 5 hour train journey to Tokyo what else is there to do but talk especially, since both of them share the same age, direction and name? Nana however, (punk Nana) has to sit in stony silence while the other Nana -(later nicknamed Hachiko due to her overbearing personality and puppyish nature) pours out her entire life (or should I say love?) story. As day's pass and the events of the train are forgotten the two Nana's find themselves face to face again as roommates and brand new c0- owners of a 2 bedroom apartment.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451551713ra/17557716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What I love about this <b> emotionally complex story </b> are that it <b>defies traditional boundaries </b> and instead actually <b>creates an image of a long lasting friendship </b> that does not center on jealousy, bitterness and passionate fights over the same boy, similar to those seen in other shoujo mangas wherein friendships are secondary to the romantic plot.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/98413.Nana__Vol__1__Nana___1_" title="Nana, Vol. 1 (Nana, #1) by Ai Yazawa" rel="nofollow noopener">Nana, Vol. 1</a> however, puts friendship on top so that we get a glimpse of their pasts through flash backs and retellings and then we are given the chance to piece all their memories and experiences in place to get the complete story. We see two alternative sides- one painting the picture of how Hachi (puppyish Nana) keeps falling in love with the wrong men and how she cannot stop her growing infatuation with cute guys and over shopping along with how she thinks that everything negative in her life is due to the "Great Demon Lord".<br>The other Nana had a very different life - the vocalist of BLAST (a hometown rock band), an orphan, a smoker and a high school dropout she projected the aura of a "tough" "broken" girl but is anything but that. Nana doesn't give up nor does she wallow in her grief instead she remains carefree and dedicated to music. She laughs easily with Hachi and her band mates (which makes me laugh in return because Hachi is just so funny!) and is like a jack of all traits. Want a table? Ask Nana because she personally crafted one for picnics and carpentry is her secret skill. Hungry? Nana also surprisingly knows how to whip up appetizing food ( even better than Hachi though she looks like the homely type). Bored? Nana can play the guitar, base and drums. Not to mention, is an amazing vocalist. SHE USES OPPORTUNITIES TO LEARN AND NOT WASTE HER LIFE AWAY.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451551713ra/17557717.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Their friendship is <b>extremely cute </b> during the beginning stages because their personalities clash at times and they are just learning about how wacky the other one is. What I love though, is that Hachi has this big girl-crush on Nana not like, in a lesbian way(even though they do share a kiss) but rather in a "you're incredibly cool and I really really want to be badass like you" way. Like all of them have such <b> realistic portrayals and incredible character development </b>- even the secondary characters, that you feel connected to all of them like a big family.<br><br>Vulnerabilities are exposed and the weak become strong. Independence, love, passion,ties,family... <br>I LOVE THIS SO MUCH. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9522064373865274209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1487008518">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425473533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer697119197319955031">Have you ever wondered what it would be like if you meet someone with the same name as you and yet is completely different from you? (Don't worry, that person is NOT your doppleganger!)<br/><br/>This, for me, was the most interesting thing about Nana. Nana Komatsu is a young woman hoping to start a new life after having gone through a lot of heartache. She moves to Tokyo and meets Nana Osaka on the train. Nana Osaka is everything she's not. She's cool, she's confident, and she's absolutely sure of what sh</span>
  <span id="freeText697119197319955031" style="display:none">Have you ever wondered what it would be like if you meet someone with the same name as you and yet is completely different from you? (Don't worry, that person is NOT your doppleganger!)<br /><br />This, for me, was the most interesting thing about Nana. Nana Komatsu is a young woman hoping to start a new life after having gone through a lot of heartache. She moves to Tokyo and meets Nana Osaka on the train. Nana Osaka is everything she's not. She's cool, she's confident, and she's absolutely sure of what she wants - to become the number 1 musician in Japan. They contrast each other in personality, beliefs, and loves, but they strangely get along. As the two spend more time together and become best friends, they face many issues regarding friendship and love. The manga is torn between their two perspectives.<br /><br />In my opinion, this was better than Paradise Kiss. I don't know why though. I mean, they pretty much are consisted of the same things except instead of fashion it's music. I feel it's more deep and darker.</span>
  <a data-text-id="697119197319955031" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText1599279061321054747" style="display:none">I guess I am not the josei type, cuz I did not like this manga too much. I heard, and read so many nice reviews about this... I even bought the anime, so I was eager to read the manga. Sadly, it was MEH to me.<br /><br />There are two Nana in this story: one of them is a naive, silly girl who fells in love with any handsome man she meets, and the result is that she keeps getting her heart broken. The other Nana is a rocker girl, not naive, tougher in looks, but in reality, had her heart broken because her boyfriend moved out to Tokyo. So both Nana have different aspects, but their stories are pretty much the same.<br /><br />So far they did not meet yet... I guess the real thing starts to happen when they do and become friends. I do not know and i think I will never do. </span>

<div id="review_2405949792" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2405949792" />
    <a title="Jack Reynolds" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27974853-jack-reynolds"><img alt="Jack Reynolds" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591532915p2/27974853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2405949792?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack Reynolds" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack Reynolds" href="/user/show/27974853-jack-reynolds">Jack Reynolds</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27974853-jack-reynolds?shelf=manga">manga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2405949792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer124052351474487258">This was a fairly good introduction to this series. Set before the two female protagonists meet each other, it follows them going to art school/performing with a band. Aside from being quite different in terms of aesthetic and personality, Nana Osaki's prologue was a more interesting read compared to Nana Komatsu (I even think Yazawa was aware of this, considering in the bonus section, she mentions the former is a stronger character). I liked the dynamic between her and Ren and the grittier feel</span>
  <span id="freeText124052351474487258" style="display:none">This was a fairly good introduction to this series. Set before the two female protagonists meet each other, it follows them going to art school/performing with a band. Aside from being quite different in terms of aesthetic and personality, Nana Osaki's prologue was a more interesting read compared to Nana Komatsu (I even think Yazawa was aware of this, considering in the bonus section, she mentions the former is a stronger character). I liked the dynamic between her and Ren and the grittier feel of her story.<br /><br />It does take a while to get into if you aren't sure what to expect. It wasn't solely because Nana Komatsu's storyline was stale at the beginning, but because this isn't the grand ol' introduction I thought it was. I'm not sure where the anime starts, but this volume would work better there if the chapters were spaced out into two episodes. That way, it would feel like the beginning of two stories that would eventually intertwine rather than ones that could conclude if you didn't want to move on with the manga.<br /><br />Overall, I'm prepared for the angst and drama no matter which path I set on, so let's see where this series will go after the two girls meet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="124052351474487258" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6ZBfc8N88Hps4g3QiS9Mr2JlBW1cKpaLfFbEP5QwVmKDt9Tg8sNrf0Dux1RJkJ9ZMWS8Gmt/T0j5xzHv/QDg9g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A/KRFjcXeA8OY5WJPV1m7gICRPl6goJbrebt3oeziXNp1RqFBqjjCiJvXw394rUYUQP9jk3XW5godxgO7oM/5w==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2698757272160558967">Ai YAZAWA (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15897480._____' title='矢沢 あい' rel='nofollow noopener'>矢沢 あい</a>) is a Japanese manga author. Her pen name comes from Japanese singer Eikichi Yazawa, of whom she is a fan.<br/><br/>Yazawa started her manga publishing life in 1985; throughout 15 years of publishing, she wrote over ten series on Ribon magazine. While most of her manga continues to be published in Japan by Shueisha, publishers of Ribon and Cookie (in which Nana is serialized), series like P</span>
  <span id="freeText2698757272160558967" style="display:none">Ai YAZAWA (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15897480._____" title="矢沢 あい" rel="nofollow noopener">矢沢 あい</a>) is a Japanese manga author. Her pen name comes from Japanese singer Eikichi Yazawa, of whom she is a fan.<br /><br />Yazawa started her manga publishing life in 1985; throughout 15 years of publishing, she wrote over ten series on Ribon magazine. While most of her manga continues to be published in Japan by Shueisha, publishers of Ribon and Cookie (in which Nana is serialized), series like Paradise Kiss now appear in other magazines such as Zipper, published by Shodensha.<br /><br />Yazawa's most famous manga include Tenshi Nanka Ja Nai (I'm Not an Angel), Gokinjo Monogatari (Neighborhood Story), Paradise Kiss, and Nana. <br />In 2003, she was awarded the Shogakukan Manga Award for Nana. <br />Some of her manga works were made into anime, and live action moves too.<br /><br />Yazawa's works are most popular among women and young girls. The storylines generally are centered on young women and their relationships, something with which her young fanbase identifies. The characters are always very stylish, and she is known especially for her hip sense of fashion. Yazawa herself attended a fashion school after high school but did not complete her studies there. Another key point is her strikingly unique, often rebellious characters, who tend to be juxtaposed against the more traditional ones.<br /><br />She has also published three artbooks.<br /><br />Works (in chronological order)<br /><br />15-nenme (1986) <br />Love Letter (1987) <br />Kaze ni Nare! (1988) <br />Escape (1988) <br />Ballad Made Soba ni Ite (1989, 2 volumes) <br />Marine Blue no Kaze ni Dakarete (1990–1991, 4 volumes) <br />Usubeni no Arashi (1992) <br />Tenshi Nanka Ja Nai (1992–1995, 8 volumes) <br />Gokinjo Monogatari (1995–1998, 7 volumes) <br />Kagen no Tsuki (1998–1999, 3 volumes) <br />Paradise Kiss (2000–2004, 5 volumes, published by Shodensha) <br />Nana (2000–ongoing, 21 volumes - on hiatus) <br />Princess Ai (2004–2006, 3 volumes) (character designs only) </span>
  <a data-text-id="2698757272160558967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
